Let me write: ```python import torch from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig CUDA_CODE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> #define SEQ_LEN 512 #define HIDDEN 256 #define NUM_HEADS 4 #define HEAD_DIM 64 #define INTERMEDIATE 1024 __global__ void electra_embeddings_kernel( const int64_t* input_ids, float* output, const float* word_embed, const float* pos_embed, const float* type_embed, const float* embed_ln_gamma, const float* embed_ln_beta, const float* proj_weight, const float* proj_bias, int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float x_shared[128]; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; int64_t token_id = input_ids[token_idx]; if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = word_embed[token_id * embed_dim + tid] + pos_embed[token_idx * embed_dim + tid] + type_embed[tid]; } __syncthreads(); float mean = 0.0f; if (tid == 0) { for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) mean += x_shared[i]; mean /= embed_dim; x_shared[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); mean = x_shared[0]; float var = 0.0f; if (tid == 0) { for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { float diff = x_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= embed_dim; x_shared[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); var = x_shared[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = (x_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * embed_ln_gamma[tid] + embed_ln_beta[tid]; } __syncthreads(); if (tid < hidden_dim) { float sum = proj_bias[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { sum += x_shared[i] * proj_weight[i * hidden_dim + tid]; } output[token_idx * hidden_dim + tid] = sum; } } __global__ void electra_qkv_kernel( const float* input, float* q, float* k, float* v, const float* W_Q, const float* b_Q, const float* W_K, const float* b_K, const float* W_V, const float* b_V, int seq_len, int hidden) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float x_shared[256]; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; if (tid < hidden) { x_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); if (tid < hidden) { float q_sum = b_Q[tid]; float k_sum = b_K[tid]; float v_sum = b_V[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float val = x_shared[i]; q_sum += val * W_Q[i * hidden + tid]; k_sum += val * W_K[i * hidden + tid]; v_sum += val * W_V[i * hidden + tid]; } q[token_idx * hidden + tid] = q_sum; k[token_idx * hidden + tid] = k_sum; v[token_idx * hidden + tid] = v_sum; } } __global__ void electra_attention_kernel( const float* q, const float* k, const float* v, const float* residual_input, float* output, const float* W_O, const float* b_O, const float* ln_gamma, const float* ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim, float scale) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int head = tid / head_dim; int lane = tid % head_dim; int sublane = lane % 32; if (token_idx >= seq_len || head >= num_heads) return; __shared__ float dot0_shared[4][SEQ_LEN]; __shared__ float dot1_shared[4][SEQ_LEN]; __shared__ float scores_shared[4][SEQ_LEN]; __shared__ float attn_out_shared[256]; __shared__ float result_shared[256]; __shared__ float partial[4][2]; __shared__ float sdata[256]; int head_offset = head * head_dim; // Load Q and compute dot products with all K float q_val = q[token_idx * hidden + head_offset + lane]; if (lane < 32) { for (int key_idx = lane; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx += 32) { float k_val = k[key_idx * hidden + head_offset + lane]; float dot = q_val * k_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (sublane == 0) dot0_shared[head][key_idx] = dot; } } else { for (int key_idx = lane - 32; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx += 32) { float k_val = k[key_idx * hidden + head_offset + lane]; float dot = q_val * k_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (sublane == 0) dot1_shared[head][key_idx] = dot; } } __syncthreads(); if (lane < 32) { for (int key_idx = lane; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx += 32) { scores_shared[head][key_idx] = (dot0_shared[head][key_idx] + dot1_shared[head][key_idx]) * scale; } } __syncthreads(); // Find max score float local_max = -INFINITY; for (int j = lane; j < seq_len; j += head_dim) { local_max = fmaxf(local_max, scores_shared[head][j]); } #pragma unroll for (int offset = 32; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, offset)); } __syncthreads(); if (sublane == 0) partial[head][lane / 32] = local_max; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { float m = partial[head][0]; if (partial[head][1] > m) m = partial[head][1]; partial[head][0] = m; } __syncthreads(); float max_score = partial[head][0]; // Compute sum of exp float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int j = lane; j < seq_len; j += head_dim) { local_sum += expf(scores_shared[head][j] - max_score); } #pragma unroll for (int offset = 32; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, offset); } __syncthreads(); if (sublane == 0) partial[head][lane / 32] = local_sum; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { partial[head][0] = partial[head][0] + partial[head][1]; } __syncthreads(); float sum_exp = partial[head][0]; float inv_sum = 1.0f / sum_exp; // Weighted sum with V float out_val = 0.0f; for (int j = lane; j < seq_len; j += head_dim) { float score = expf(scores_shared[head][j] - max_score) * inv_sum; float v_val = v[j * hidden + head_offset + lane]; out_val += score * v_val; } attn_out_shared[head_offset + lane] = out_val; __syncthreads(); // Output projection float proj = b_O[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { proj += attn_out_shared[i] * W_O[i * hidden + tid]; } // Add residual proj += residual_input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; result_shared[tid] = proj; __syncthreads(); // LayerNorm float ln_val = (tid < hidden) ? result_shared[tid] : 0.0f; sdata[tid] = ln_val; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 128) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 128]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 64) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 64]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 32) { sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 32]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 16]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 8]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 4]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 2]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 1]; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0] / hidden; float var_val = (tid < hidden) ? (result_shared[tid] - mean) * (result_shared[tid] - mean) : 0.0f; sdata[tid] = var_val; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 128) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 128]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 64) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 64]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 32) { sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 32]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 16]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 8]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 4]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 2]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 1]; } __syncthreads(); float var = sdata[0] / hidden; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (result_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } __global__ void electra_ffn_kernel( const float* input, float* output, const float* W_inter, const float* b_inter, const float* W_out, const float* b_out, const float* ln_gamma, const float* ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int intermediate_size) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; __shared__ float input_shared[256]; __shared__ float inter_shared[1024]; __shared__ float result_shared[256]; __shared__ float sdata[256]; if (tid < hidden) { input_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); if (tid < 256) { for (int j = 0; j < 4; j++) { int out_idx = tid + j * 256; float sum = b_inter[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += input_shared[i] * W_inter[i * intermediate_size + out_idx]; } sum = 0.5f * sum * (1.0f + erff(sum * 0.70710678118f)); inter_shared[out_idx] = sum; } } __syncthreads(); if (tid < hidden) { float sum = b_out[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < intermediate_size; i++) { sum += inter_shared[i] * W_out[i * hidden + tid]; } sum += input_shared[tid]; result_shared[tid] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // LayerNorm float ln_val = (tid < hidden) ? result_shared[tid] : 0.0f; sdata[tid] = ln_val; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 128) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 128]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 64) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 64]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 32) { sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 32]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 16]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 8]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 4]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 2]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 1]; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0] / hidden; float var_val = (tid < hidden) ? (result_shared[tid] - mean) * (result_shared[tid] - mean) : 0.0f; sdata[tid] = var_val; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 128) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 128]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 64) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 64]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 32) { sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 32]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 16]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 8]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 4]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 2]; sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 1]; } __syncthreads(); float var = sdata[0] / hidden; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (result_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } // Host wrapper functions void electra_embeddings_forward( at::Tensor input_ids, at::Tensor output, at::Tensor word_embed, at::Tensor pos_embed, at::Tensor type_embed, at::Tensor embed_ln_gamma, at::Tensor embed_ln_beta, at::Tensor proj_weight, at::Tensor proj_bias, int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim) { cudaStream_t stream = at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream().stream(); electra_embeddings_kernel<<<seq_len, 256, 0, stream>>>( input_ids.data_ptr<int64_t>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), word_embed.data_ptr<float>(), pos_embed.data_ptr<float>(), type_embed.data_ptr<float>(), embed_ln_gamma.data_ptr<float>(), embed_ln_beta.data_ptr<float>(), proj_weight.data_ptr<float>(), proj_bias.data_ptr<float>(), seq_len, vocab_size, embed_dim, hidden_dim); } void electra_qkv_forward( at::Tensor input, at::Tensor q, at::Tensor k, at::Tensor v, at::Tensor W_Q, at::Tensor b_Q, at::Tensor W_K, at::Tensor b_K, at::Tensor W_V, at::Tensor b_V, int seq_len, int hidden) { cudaStream_t stream = at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream().stream(); electra_qkv_kernel<<<seq_len, 256, 0, stream>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), q.data_ptr<float>(), k.data_ptr<float>(), v.data_ptr<float>(), W_Q.data_ptr<float>(), b_Q.data_ptr<float>(), W_K.data_ptr<float>(), b_K.data_ptr<float>(), W_V.data_ptr<float>(), b_V.data_ptr<float>(), seq_len, hidden); } void electra_attention_forward( at::Tensor q, at::Tensor k, at::Tensor v, at::Tensor residual_input, at::Tensor output, at::Tensor W_O, at::Tensor b_O, at::Tensor ln_gamma, 'electra_attention_forward', 'electra_ffn_forward' ], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', '--use_fast_math'], verbose=False ) class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, model_name, config): super().__init__() self.model_name = model_name self.config = config # Load the reference model to extract weights self.ref_model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, config=config) self.ref_model.eval() # Extract model architecture params self.hidden_size = config.hidden_size self.num_hidden_layers = config.num_hidden_layers self.num_attention_heads = config.num_attention_heads self.intermediate_size = config.intermediate_size self.vocab_size = config.vocab_size self.embedding_size = getattr(config, 'embedding_size', self.hidden_size) self.max_position_embeddings = embeddings.LayerNorm.bias.data.to(device).contiguous() # Embedding projection if needed if hasattr(self.ref_model.electra, 'embeddings_project'): proj = self.ref_model.electra.embeddings_project self.proj_weight = proj.weight.data.to(device).contiguous() self.proj_bias = proj.bias.data.to(device).contiguous() self.has_projection = True else: # No projection, create identity self.proj_weight = torch.eye(self.hidden_size, self.embedding_size, device=device, dtype=torch.float32).contiguous() self.proj_bias = torch.zeros(self.hidden_size, device=device, dtype=torch.float32).contiguous() self.has_projection = True # We'll still do the matmul # Extract layer weights self.layer_weights = [] for layer in self.ref_model.electra.encoder.layer: layer_params = { 'W_Q': layer.attention.self.query.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'b_Q': layer.attention.self.query.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'W_K': layer.attention.self.key.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'b_K': layer.attention.self.key.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'W_V': layer.attention.self.value.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), layer.attention.output.dense.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'ln_attn_gamma': layer.attention.output.LayerNorm.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'ln_attn_beta': layer.attention.output.LayerNorm.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'W_inter': layer.intermediate.dense.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'b_inter': layer.intermediate.dense.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'W_out': layer.output.dense.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'b_out': layer.output.dense.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'ln_out_gamma': layer.output.LayerNorm.weight.data.to(device).contiguous(), 'ln_out_beta': layer.output.LayerNorm.bias.data.to(device).contiguous(), } self.layer_weights.append(layer_params) # Extract self.hidden_size, device=device, dtype=torch.float32) def forward(self, x): batch_size, seq_len = x.shape assert batch_size == 1 device = x.device # Embedding + projection self.proj_bias, seq_len, self.vocab_size, self.embedding_size, self.hidden_size ) # Ping-pong between scratch1 and scratch2 current = self.scratch1 next_buf = self.scratch2 for i in w['W_K'], w['b_K'], w['W_V'], w['b_V'], seq_len, self.hidden_size ) electra_cuda.electra_attention_forward( self.q_buf[:seq_len], self.k_buf[:seq_len], self.v_buf[:seq_len], current[:seq_len], LM head: [seq_len, hidden] @ [hidden, vocab_size] + bias Given seq_len=511, hidden=256, intermediate=1024: - QKV: 511 x 256 @ 256 x 256 -> small gemm - Attention: 511 x 64 dot products per head, 4 heads -> mainly memory bound - FFN intermediate: 511 x 256 @ 256 x 1024 - FFN output: 511 x 1024 @ 1024 x 256 - LM head: 511 x 256 @ 256 x 30522 -> this is the biggest The main speedup opportunity is reducing kernel launch and memory transfer overhead by fusing operations. Let me write a simplified but correct kernel approach. I'll use individual kernels per layer but fuse within each layer component (QKV, attention, FFN). Or better yet, let me identify what PyTorch does inefficiently. The reference model does many small kernel launches (one per operation). Each attention layer alone involves: Q, K, V linear projections (3 kernels), reshape/transpose, attention score computation (batched matmul), softmax, value aggregation, output projection, residual add, layer norm. That's a lot of kernels. My approach: fuse each layer into as few kernels as possible: 1. One kernel for QKV projection (reads input once, outputs Q, K, V) 2. One kernel for attention + output projection + residual + ln (the tricky one) 3. One kernel for FFN + residual + ln For the attention kernel, I need to be very careful. For small hidden_dim=64 per head and num_heads=4, a block can process one query position across all heads, or one head across all query positions. Given seq_len=511 and we're on H100, we could launch ~511 blocks, each handling one query position. Within each block, we compute all head attention. But all heads share the same K and V (reshaped). So: - Block per query position - Within block, for each head, compute attention scores across all key positions - Use shared memory for K and V values? For 511 x 256 floats = ~512KB, too much for shared memory. - Or load K and V from global memory directly For numerical accuracy, my main concern is: 1. Layer norm: using population variance or sample variance? PyTorch uses `1e-12` eps typically. BERT-style models use `eps=1e-12`. 2. GELU approximation: `0.5 * x * (1 + erf(x / sqrt(2)))` is the exact formula. 3. Attention: use scaled dot product with softmax, and ensure numerical stability with max subtraction. With one thread per head_dim element, we need to reduce within the thread block for each key position. For head_dim=64 and blockSize=64 (one warp or two warps), we can reduce using warp shuffles: - For key_idx from 0 to seq_len-1: - Each thread i computes q[i] * k[key_idx][i] - Reduce across threads using shuffle - The result is the attention score for (query, key) Then we need to: - Track max score for numerical stability - Compute softmax probabilities - Compute weighted sum of values One issue: we need two passes (one for max, one for exp and sum), then a third for weighted values. Here's a better approach for the attention kernel: Since seq_len=511 is not huge, we can store attention scores in shared memory: - `scores[seq_len]` - one float per key position But with 511 floats = ~2KB of shared memory per block, and we also need `attn_out[head_dim]` and some temp space. Total is very manageable! So for each query position + head: 1. Each thread computes partial dot products 2. We use a loop: for key_idx in 0..seq_len-1: - Load K[key_idx * hidden + head_offset + tid] - Compute dot = q_val * k_val - Reduce across threads (warp shuffle) - Store score in shared memory 3. Now all scores are in shared memory 4. Compute max over scores (parallel reduction) 5. Compute softmax denominators 6. Compute weighted sum of V values 7. Store attention output per head_dim This is clean and correct. Let me write it out properly. One important note: the reduction across threads with shuffle. For head_dim=64, we can have 64 threads per block. For the dot product reduction: ```cuda float dot = q_val * k_val; // Reduce within warp #pragma unroll for (int offset = 32; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); ``` Wait, for head_dim=64, if blockDim.x=64, we have 2 warps. `__shfl_xor_sync` only works within a warp. Compilation For compilation, I'll use the pattern: declarations in `cpp_sources`, implementations in `cuda_sources`. Let me write this out now. OK here's my plan for the attention kernel: ```cpp // In cuda_sources __global__ __launch_bounds__(32) void attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, const float* __restrict__ residual, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ W_O, const float* __restrict__ b_O, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int head = blockIdx.y; int lane = threadIdx.x; int head_offset = head * head_dim; int elem0 = head_offset + lane * 2; int elem1 = elem0 + 1; float q0 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem0]; float q1 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem1]; __shared__ float scores[512]; const float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)head_dim); // Compute attention scores for (int key_idx = lane; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx += 32) { float k0 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float k1 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; float dot = q0 * k0 + q1 * k1; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; } __syncwarp(); // Two more warps needed if seq_len > 32... but we used loop with stride 32 // Wait, each key_idx is handled by one warp. The scores are written by lane 0. // But what about key_idx that aren't handled by lane 0 specifically? // The loop is: for key_idx = lane; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx += 32 // For lane=0: key_idx = 0, 32, 64, ... // For lane=1: key_idx = 1, 33, 65, ... // Each lane computes the dot for its key_idx and writes it. This works! // But wait, the __shfl_down_sync returns the result to ALL threads in the warp. // Then lane == 0 writes. But what if lane 1 also tries to write key_idx=1? // Actually, in the loop: // lane=0: key_idx=0, writes scores[0] // lane=1: key_idx=1, writes scores[1] // etc. // But the shfl_down reduces across the warp, so after reduction, dot in lane=1 // is the sum for key_idx=1 (from all threads computing that specific key_idx). // Wait no, each thread computes q0*k0+q1*k1 for a DIFFERENT key_idx. // The shfl_down sums across threads, but the k values are different for each thread! // This is WRONG! ``` Oh no, I made a critical error. If each thread loads a different K (for a different key_idx), then `__shfl_down` sums q*k values across different key positions, which is completely wrong! The correct approach: 1. For a fixed key_idx, ALL threads should load K for that SAME key_idx 2. Then compute q*k, reduce across threads 3. Store result 4. Move to next key_idx So: ```cuda for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float k0 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float k1 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; float dot = q0 * k0 + q1 * k1; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; } ``` This is correct! All threads load the same K (same key_idx), compute partial dot products, reduce within warp. Then lane 0 stores. This requires seq_len iterations over all key positions. For seq_len=511, that's 511 iterations. With 32 threads and 2 elements each, we do 64 FMAs per iteration, plus shuffle overhead. Overall ~32K FMAs per head per query. For 4 heads and 511 queries, that's ~65M FMAs. Very manageable. Then softmax: ```cuda // Find max float local_max = -INFINITY; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, scores[i]); for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, offset)); float max_score = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, 0); // Compute exp and sum float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_sum += expf(scores[i] - max_score); for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, offset); float sum_exp = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, 0); // Compute weighted V sum float out0 = 0.0f; float out1 = 0.0f; for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float prob = expf(scores[key_idx] - max_score) / sum_exp; float v0 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float v1 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; out0 += prob * v0; out1 += prob * v1; } ``` Wait, there's an issue with the prob computation. Each thread doesn't have access to all `scores` unless they're in shared memory and we sync. Let me put `scores` in shared memory and load it in the loop: ```cuda __shared__ float scores[512]; // shared memory // ...compute scores... __syncwarp(); float out0 = 0.0f; float out1 = 0.0f; for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float prob = expf(scores[key_idx] - max_score) / sum_exp; float v0 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float v1 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; out0 += prob * v0; out1 += prob * v1; } ``` This works because scores are in shared memory and accessible to all threads in the block. Since we only have 32 threads per block (1 warp), __syncwarp() is sufficient. Now, after computing attention outputs for all heads, we need to do output projection + residual + layer norm. We can do this in the same kernel or a separate one. Let's do it in the same kernel for better fusion. For output projection: ```cuda __shared__ float attn_shared[256]; // attention output for this token // Each block writes to attn_shared[elem0] = out0, attn_shared[elem1] = out1 if (lane < 16) { // Actually all 32 threads write 2 elements each = 64 elements // This only writes 64 elements, but hidden=256 } ``` Oh, each block only computes one head (64 elements). To get the full attention output (256 elements), we need to run 4 blocks per token (one per head) and somehow aggregate. After all 4 blocks finish, we need to launch another phase. But CUDA doesn't have inter-block synchronization. Options: 1. Use two kernels: attention kernel outputs per-head results to global memory, then a second kernel does output projection + residual + ln 2. Use a grid sync (cooperative groups) - complex 3. Have each block compute all heads sequentially Option 3 is cleanest for a fused kernel. Instead of [seq_len, num_heads] grid, use [seq_len] grid with more threads per block. Each block handles all heads for one query position. For hidden=256, num_heads=4, head_dim=64: - Block size: 64 threads (handles one head, or process two heads with two warps) - Actually, let's use 128 threads = 2 warps per head... no. Better: 64 threads per block, process all 4 heads sequentially. Per head: - 64 threads compute the attention output for that head - Reduce and store in shared memory - Loop to next head After all heads: - 64 threads do the output projection (but hidden=256, so we need more) - Actually, 64 threads can each compute 4 output features Wait, 64 threads x 4 features = 256 features. So each thread can handle 4 elements of the output projection. Let me redesign: - Grid: [seq_len] blocks - Block: 64 threads - Shared memory: - input_qkv[256] - for storing Q/K/V elements? Actually we read from global memory. - attn_out[256] - accumulated attention output across all heads - scores[512] - attention scores for current head This is getting complex but manageable. Actually, let me simplify even further. Given seq_len=511 and hidden=256: - Each query position needs ~511*64 + 511*64 + 511*64 = ~98K reads from global memory for QKV - Plus intermediate writes For better cache utilization, processing all heads for one query in one block is good because K and V are reused across heads. Let me write out the full attention kernel with this design: ```cuda __global__ void fused_attention( const float* q, const float* k, const float* v, const float* residual, float* output, const float* W_O, const float* b_O, const float* ln_gamma, const float* ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; // 0..63 int lane = tid % 32; int warp = tid / 32; __shared__ float attn_out[256]; __shared__ float scores[512]; __shared__ float sdata[256]; // Each thread handles 4 elements (since 64 threads * 4 = 256) // But for attention, we process one head at a time // Each warp handles 2 elements per thread = 64 elements = one head const float scale = rsqrtf((float)head_dim); for (int h = 0; h < num_heads; h++) { int head_offset = h * head_dim; float q0 = q[token_idx * hidden + head_offset + warp * 32 + lane]; // This gives 64 threads x 1 element = 64 elements... but warp is 0 or 1 // Hmm, 2 warps * 32 lanes = 64 elements // Wait, for head_dim=64, if tid goes 0..63: // element = head_offset + tid float q_val = q[token_idx * hidden + head_offset + tid]; // Compute scores for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float k_val = k[key_idx * hidden + head_offset + tid]; float dot = q_val * k_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; // Only lane 0 writes? But there are 2 warps! // Warp 0 writes scores[key_idx] and so does warp 1. This is a race condition! } } ``` The issue is with 2 warps: both warps would try to write to `scores[key_idx]`. I need one warp to compute and write. Solution: have ONE warp compute all attention scores for a head. Since head_dim=64, one warp of 32 threads can each handle 2 elements. Redesign: - Block: 32 threads (1 warp) - Grid: [seq_len, num_heads] - After all attention heads are computed, we need to run output projection + residual + ln This is a 2-kernel approach: 1. Kernel 1: [seq_len, num_heads] blocks of 32 threads -> compute attention output per head, write to global memory 2. Kernel 2: [seq_len] blocks -> read attention outputs, apply O_proj, residual, ln Actually, we can keep the QKV projection separate too: 1. Kernel: QKV projection (one kernel, all 3 projections fused) 2. Kernel: Attention (per head per query, write attn_out to global) 3. Kernel: Output proj + residual + ln 4. Kernel: FFN + residual + ln Or even simpler: 1. Fused QKV 2. PyTorch attention (using batched matmul) 3. Fused output + residual + ln 4. Fused FFN Given the memory bandwidth is the main bottleneck and my custom kernels will reduce memory round-trips, even this simpler design should be faster. Actually, wait. If I use PyTorch for attention, it will be using optimized cuBLAS/cuDNN kernels which are very fast. But the overhead of multiple kernel launches and memory round-trips might still make it slower than a custom fused approach. Let me just go with a fully custom forward pass for maximum fusion. If correctness is tricky, I'll debug iteratively. Let me write the simplest correct implementation: For each operation, I'll use a separate kernel to keep things manageable: 1. `embed_proj_kernel`: embedding lookup + layer norm + projection 2. `qkv_kernel`: fused Q/K/V projections 3. `attention_kernel`: per-head attention -> writes per-head results 4. `attn_out_kernel`: output projection + residual + ln 5. `ffn_kernel`: intermediate + GELU + output + residual + ln 6. LM head using PyTorch matmul (since vocab_size is large and cuBLAS is very optimized) Let me now carefully write these kernels with correct numerical behavior. For the attention kernel, I'll use [seq_len, num_heads] blocks of 32 threads each: - Each thread handles 2 elements (head_dim=64 / 32 = 2) - For each key position, all threads load K for the same key position - Warp shuffle to reduce partial sums - Lane 0 writes to shared memory - Then softmax and weighted sum ```cuda __global__ __launch_bounds__(32) void attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ attn_out, // [seq_len, hidden] int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int head = blockIdx.y; int lane = threadIdx.x; int head_offset = head * head_dim; int elem0 = head_offset + lane * 2; int elem1 = elem0 + 1; float q0 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem0]; float q1 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem1]; __shared__ float scores[512]; const float scale = rsqrtf((float)head_dim); for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float k0 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float k1 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; float dot = q0 * k0 + q1 * k1; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; } __syncwarp(); // Max score float local_max = -1e9f; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, scores[i]); #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, offset)); float max_score = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, 0); // Sum of exp float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_sum += expf(scores[i] - max_score); #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, offset); float sum_exp = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, 0); float inv_sum = 1.0f / sum_exp; // Weighted sum of values float out0 = 0.0f; float out1 = 0.0f; for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float prob = expf(scores[key_idx] - max_score) * inv_sum; float v0 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float v1 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; out0 += prob * v0; out1 += prob * v1; } attn_out[token_idx * hidden + elem0] = out0; attn_out[token_idx * hidden + elem1] = out1; } ``` Wait, there's a crucial bug: `scores[key_idx]` is only updated by lane 0, but all threads read `scores[key_idx]` in the loop. Since we're in the same warp, and lane 0 writes to shared memory, do the other threads see it immediately? In CUDA, shared memory writes are visible to all threads in the block after a memory fence or barrier. For a single warp, `__syncwarp()` should be sufficient. But I only call `__syncwarp()` once after the score computation loop. Within the loop where I read `scores[key_idx]`, the write might not be visible yet because: 1. `scores[key_idx]` was potentially written by a different iteration of the outer loop (same key_idx) 2. Actually, within the same loop iteration, lane 0 writes to shared memory and then all threads read from it in the next statement The issue is that within a single warp, a `__syncwarp()` is indeed needed between the write and read for correctness. But actually for a single warp (32 threads), if lane 0 writes and all other threads in that same warp read, is `__syncwarp()` needed? Yes, for correctness, `__syncwarp()` or `__threadfence_block()` should be used to guarantee memory ordering within a warp. However, in practice on modern GPUs, a warp executes in lockstep, so if lane 0 writes and subsequently all threads read, the write should be visible because: 1. The write instruction completes before the next instruction in the same warp (SIMT execution). Actually, for shared memory within a single warp, writes are guaranteed to be visible to other threads in the same warp without explicit synchronization IF the write and read are separated by at least one instruction and there are no bank conflicts. But to be safe, I'll add `__syncwarp()` inside the loop or restructure to avoid the issue. Actually, a cleaner approach: after computing all scores, do `__syncwarp()`. Then in the subsequent loops (max, sum, weighted values), all reads are from already-written shared memory and `__syncwarp()` was already called. This is correct. Wait, looking at the code again: - The first loop writes `scores[key_idx]` for key_idx from 0 to seq_len-1 - After the loop, `__syncwarp()` ensures all writes are visible - The max loop reads from `scores` - correct - The sum loop reads from `scores` - correct - The weighted sum loop reads from `scores` - correct But there's another issue: when seq_len > 32, each thread only writes some scores (lane 0 writes key_idx 0, but what about key_idx 1?). Oh wait, in the first loop: ```cuda for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { ... if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; } ``` Only lane 0 writes! But the dot is computed by all threads and reduced using shuffle. After reduction, all threads have the same value in `dot`. Lane 0 writes it. For all key_idx positions, lane 0 does the write. This is correct because each key_idx iteration computes the score for that key position, and lane 0 stores it. Wait, but `dot` after shuffle is the total sum across all threads. So all threads have the same value. Lane 0 writes it. This is correct. Another issue: `__shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset)` accumulates the dot product across lanes. After the loop, all lanes have the total sum. Lane 0 writes to shared memory. This is correct. Actually, let me double check. `__shfl_xor_sync` does a butterfly shuffle. `dot += __shfl_xor_sync(..., dot, 16)` means lane i gets value from lane i^16 and adds to dot. After all offsets, every lane has the sum of all lanes. Yes, this is a correct reduction within a warp. Now for the output projection + layer norm kernel: ```cuda __global__ void attn_output_kernel( const float* __restrict__ attn_out, const float* __restrict__ residual, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ W_O, const float* __restrict__ b_O, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float temp_shared[256]; __shared__ float shared_sums[2]; // for mean and var if (tid < hidden) { temp_shared[tid] = attn_out[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Output projection: temp_shared @ W_O + b_O // Then add residual if (tid < hidden) { float sum = b_O[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += temp_shared[i] * W_O[i * hidden + tid]; } sum += residual[token_idx * hidden + tid]; temp_shared[tid] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm if (tid == 0) { float mean = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) mean += temp_shared[i]; mean /= hidden; shared_sums[0] = mean; } if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float diff = temp_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= hidden; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (temp_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } ``` For this kernel, I'll use block size = 256 threads, grid = seq_len. Wait, there's a subtle race condition in the layer norm code. Thread 0 computes mean and writes to shared_sums[0]. Then thread 1 tries to read shared_sums[0] before it's ready! Let me fix: ```cuda if (tid == 0) { // compute mean shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; // compute var shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); ``` That's correct. Alternatively, I can use a single thread for both mean and var to simplify, since the reduction is very small (256 elements). Or use parallel reduction. But for now, sequential with proper sync is fine. For the FFN kernel: ```cuda __global__ void ffn_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ W_inter, const float* __restrict__ b_inter, const float* __restrict__ W_out, const float* __restrict__ b_out, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int intermediate_size) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float input_shared[256]; __shared__ float inter_shared[1024]; __shared__ float temp_shared[256]; __shared__ float shared_sums[2]; if (tid < hidden) { input_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Intermediate: input @ W_inter + b_inter if (tid < intermediate_size) { float sum = b_inter[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += input_shared[i] * W_inter[i * intermediate_size + tid]; } // GELU sum = 0.5f * sum * (1.0f + erff(sum * 0.70710678118f)); inter_shared[tid] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Output: inter @ W_out + b_out + residual if (tid < hidden) { float sum = b_out[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < intermediate_size; i++) { sum += inter_shared[i] * W_out[i * hidden + tid]; } sum += input_shared[tid]; temp_shared[tid] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm if (tid == 0) { float mean = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) mean += temp_shared[i]; mean /= hidden; shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float diff = temp_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= hidden; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (temp_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } ``` For this, I'll use block size = max(intermediate_size, hidden) = 1024 threads. But wait, H100 limits are: - Max threads per block: 1024 - Max shared memory per block: 227KB My shared memory usage: - input_shared[256] = 1KB - inter_shared[1024] = 4KB - temp_shared[256] = 1KB - shared_sums[2] = 8B Total = ~6KB. Very manageable. But 1024 threads is the maximum. For grid = seq_len = 511 blocks, that's 511 blocks * 1024 threads = ~523K threads total. On H100 with many SMs, this is fine. Wait, but I need to be careful: one block with 1024 threads uses a lot of registers. With 64K registers per SM and 64 registers per thread (typical), that's exactly 1024 threads per SM. So we can run 1 block per SM. H100 has 132 SMs (I think), so 132 blocks in parallel. 511 blocks total means ~4 waves. Not bad. Actually, for many operations, only 256 threads are active (since hidden=256). The intermediate computation needs 1024 threads. Let me see if I should use a different block size. Alternative: use 256 threads for everything, and have each thread handle multiple intermediate features. Or use dynamic loop unrolling. With 256 threads: - Intermediate: each thread handles intermediate_size/256 = 1024/256 = 4 features This is actually better for occupancy! Let me redesign: ```cuda // With 256 threads for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < intermediate_size; out_idx += blockDim.x) { float sum = b_inter[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += input_shared[i] * W_inter[i * intermediate_size + out_idx]; } sum = 0.5f * sum * (1.0f + erff(sum * 0.70710678118f)); inter_shared[out_idx] = sum; } ``` This is cleaner and gives better occupancy. With 256 threads, each block uses fewer registers, allowing more concurrent blocks per SM. Let me now think about the QKV kernel: ```cuda __global__ void qkv_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ q, float* __restrict__ k, float* __restrict__ v, const float* __restrict__ W_Q, const float* __restrict__ b_Q, const float* __restrict__ W_K, const float* __restrict__ b_K, const float* __restrict__ W_V, const float* __restrict__ b_V, int seq_len, int hidden) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float x_shared[256]; if (tid < hidden) { x_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden; out_idx += blockDim.x) { float q_sum = b_Q[out_idx]; float k_sum = b_K[out_idx]; float v_sum = b_V[out_idx]; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float val = x_shared[i]; q_sum += val * W_Q[i * hidden + out_idx]; k_sum += val * W_K[i * hidden + out_idx]; v_sum += val * W_V[i * hidden + out_idx]; } q[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = q_sum; k[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = k_sum; v[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = v_sum; } } ``` Here with 256 threads, each thread computes one output feature per projection. So for hidden=256 and blockDim=256, each thread computes exactly one output feature. This is very efficient! For the embedding kernel: ```cuda __global__ void embed_kernel( const int64_t* __restrict__ input_ids, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ word_embed, const float* __restrict__ pos_embed, const float* __restrict__ type_embed, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, const float* __restrict__ proj_weight, const float* __restrict__ proj_bias, int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float x_shared[256]; __shared__ float shared_sums[2]; int64_t token_id = input_ids[token_idx]; if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = word_embed[token_id * embed_dim + tid] + pos_embed[token_idx * embed_dim + tid] + type_embed[tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm if (tid == 0) { float mean = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) mean += x_shared[i]; mean /= embed_dim; shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { float diff = x_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= embed_dim; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = (x_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Projection if (tid < hidden_dim) { float sum = proj_bias[tid]; for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { sum += x_shared[i] * proj_weight[i * hidden_dim + tid]; } output[token_idx * hidden_dim + tid] = sum; } } ``` With embed_dim=128 and hidden_dim=256, we can use 256 threads. For all these kernels, I use W as column-major (transposed) such that `W[i * N + j]` corresponds to the weight from input i to output j. This is because we iterate over input i in the inner loop and write to output j. Wait, in PyTorch `nn.Linear`, `output = input @ W^T + b`, where W has shape [out_features, in_features]. So for `output[j] = sum_i input[i] * W[j, i]`. In my kernel, I use `W[i * hidden + j]` which implies the transpose is already applied: `W^T[i, j] = W[j, i]`. So `output[j] = sum_i input[i] * W^T[i, j] = sum_i input[i] * W_T[i * hidden + j]`. So I should store `W_Q_t = W_Q.t()`, `W_K_t = W_K.t()`, etc. Yes, and I already did that in my init code: `layer.attention.self.query.weight.data.t().contiguous().to(device)`. So that's correct. Now, one thing I need to be careful about: in PyTorch, `nn.Linear` weights are stored as [out_features, in_features]. When I do `weight.data.t()`, I get [in_features, out_features]. Then `W_t[i * out_features + j]` = original weight[j, i]. And in the matmul: `sum_i input[i] * W_t[i * out_features + j] = sum_i input[i] * original_weight[j, i]`, which is correct for `output = input @ W^T`. Great. My matmul does accumulation in a specific order (i loop). PyTorch/cuBLAS might do it in a different order (e.g., tile-based). This introduces small differences due to floating-point associativity. 2. The tolerance is 1e-4 for fp32. For a model with 12 layers, errors can accumulate. To mitigate: 1. Use the same accumulation order as much as possible. 2. Be careful with intermediate precision. PyTorch's softmax is: ```python max_score = scores.max(dim=-1, keepdim=True) exp_scores = torch.exp(scores - max_score) sum_exp = exp_scores.sum(dim=-1, keepdim=True) probs = exp_scores / sum_exp ``` In my kernel: 1. I compute max_score correctly using reduction 2. I compute `expf(scores[i] - max_score)` and sum them 3. I divide by sum_exp This should match PyTorch's softmax exactly for the same input scores. For each of 12 layers: a. `qkv_kernel`: `[seq_len, hidden] -> q, k, v` (fused QKV projection) b. `attention_kernel`: `q, k, v -> [seq_len, hidden]` (attention per head) c. `attn_output_kernel`: `[seq_len, hidden], residual -> [seq_len, hidden]` (output proj + residual + ln) d. `ffn_kernel`: `[seq_len, hidden] -> [seq_len, hidden]` (FFN + residual + ln) 3. `torch.matmul(hidden_states, lm_head_weight.t()) + lm_head_bias` -> logits For numerical stability and correctness, let me also add a tiny test in init to print model architecture. Here's my final code structure: ```python import torch from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline # CUDA kernel code (cuda_sources) CUDA_CODE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> __global__ void embed_kernel(...) { ... } __global__ void qkv_kernel(...) { ... } __global__ void attention_kernel(...) { ... } __global__ void attn_out_kernel(...) { ... } __global__ void ffn_kernel(...) { ... } torch::Tensor electra_embed_forward(...) { auto output = torch::empty(...); embed_kernel<<<...>>>(...); return output; } void electra_qkv_forward(...) { qkv_kernel<<<...>>>(...); } void electra_attention_forward(...) { attention_kernel<<<...>>>(...); } void electra_attn_out_forward(...) { attn_out_kernel<<<...>>>(...); } void electra_ffn_forward(...) { ffn_kernel<<<...>>>(...); } ''' # C++ declarations (cpp_sources) CPP_CODE = ''' #include <torch/extension.h> torch::Tensor electra_embed_forward( torch::Tensor input_ids, torch::Tensor word_embed, torch::Tensor pos_embed, torch::Tensor type_embed, torch::Tensor ln_gamma, torch::Tensor ln_beta, torch::Tensor proj_weight, torch::Tensor proj_bias, int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim); void electra_qkv_forward( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor q, torch::Tensor k, torch::Tensor v, torch::Tensor W_Q, torch::Tensor b_Q, torch::Tensor W_K, torch::Tensor b_K, torch::Tensor W_V, torch::Tensor b_V, int seq_len, int hidden); void electra_attention_forward( torch::Tensor q, torch::Tensor k, torch::Tensor v, torch::Tensor attn_out, int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim); void electra_attn_out_forward( torch::Tensor attn_out, torch::Tensor residual, torch::Tensor output, torch::Tensor W_O, torch::Tensor b_O, torch::Tensor ln_gamma, torch::Tensor ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden); void electra_ffn_forward( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor output, torch::Tensor W_inter, torch::Tensor b_inter, torch::Tensor W_out, torch::Tensor b_out, torch::Tensor ln_gamma, torch::Tensor ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int intermediate_size); ''' _electra_cuda = load_inline( name='electra_custom', cpp_sources=CPP_CODE, cuda_sources=CUDA_CODE, functions=[ 'electra_embed_forward', 'electra_qkv_forward', 'electra_attention_forward', 'electra_attn_out_forward', 'electra_ffn_forward' ], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3'], verbose=False ) ``` Wait, do I need `extra_cflags` too? For cpp_sources, I don't need any special flags. For cuda_sources, `-O3` is good. Let me now carefully write all the kernels. I'll be very precise. Kernel 1: embed_kernel ```cuda __global__ void embed_kernel( const int64_t* __restrict__ input_ids, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ word_embed, const float* __restrict__ pos_embed, const float* __restrict__ type_embed, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, const float* __restrict__ proj_weight, const float* __restrict__ proj_bias, int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int nthread = blockDim.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; __shared__ float x_shared[256]; __shared__ float shared_sums[4]; int64_t token_id = input_ids[token_idx]; if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = word_embed[token_id * embed_dim + tid] + pos_embed[token_idx * embed_dim + tid] + type_embed[tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm float mean = 0.0f; if (tid == 0) { for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) mean += x_shared[i]; mean /= embed_dim; shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; if (tid == 1) { for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { float diff = x_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= embed_dim; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < embed_dim) { x_shared[tid] = (x_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Projection for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden_dim; out_idx += nthread) { float sum = proj_bias[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) { sum += x_shared[i] * proj_weight[i * hidden_dim + out_idx]; } output[token_idx * hidden_dim + out_idx] = sum; } } ``` Kernel 2: qkv_kernel ```cuda __global__ void qkv_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ q, float* __restrict__ k, float* __restrict__ v, const float* __restrict__ W_Q, const float* __restrict__ b_Q, const float* __restrict__ W_K, const float* __restrict__ b_K, const float* __restrict__ W_V, const float* __restrict__ b_V, int seq_len, int hidden) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int nthread = blockDim.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* x_shared = smem; if (tid < hidden) { x_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden; out_idx += nthread) { float q_sum = b_Q[out_idx]; float k_sum = b_K[out_idx]; float v_sum = b_V[out_idx]; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float val = x_shared[i]; q_sum += val * W_Q[i * hidden + out_idx]; k_sum += val * W_K[i * hidden + out_idx]; v_sum += val * W_V[i * hidden + out_idx]; } q[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = q_sum; k[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = k_sum; v[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = v_sum; } } ``` Wait, I'm using `extern __shared__ float smem[]` with dynamic shared memory. I need to pass the size in the kernel launch: `<<<seq_len, 256, hidden * sizeof(float)>>>`. That's fine. Kernel 3: attention_kernel ```cuda __global__ __launch_bounds__(32) void attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ attn_out, int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int head = blockIdx.y; int lane = threadIdx.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len || head >= num_heads || lane >= 32) return; int head_offset = head * head_dim; int elem0 = head_offset + lane * 2; int elem1 = elem0 + 1; float q0 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem0]; float q1 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem1]; __shared__ float scores[512]; const float scale = rsqrtf((float)head_dim); for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float k0 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float k1 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; float dot = q0 * k0 + q1 * k1; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); if (lane == 0) scores[key_idx] = dot * scale; } __syncwarp(); // Max score float local_max = -1e9f; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, scores[i]); #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, offset)); float max_score = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_max, 0); // Sum of exp float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32) local_sum += expf(scores[i] - max_score); #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, offset); float sum_exp = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, 0); float inv_sum = 1.0f / sum_exp; // Weighted sum float out0 = 0.0f; float out1 = 0.0f; for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) { float prob = expf(scores[key_idx] - max_score) * inv_sum; float v0 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem0]; float v1 = v[key_idx * hidden + elem1]; out0 += prob * v0; out1 += prob * v1; } attn_out[token_idx * hidden + elem0] = out0; attn_out[token_idx * hidden + elem1] = out1; } ``` Wait, there's a concern about `__syncwarp()` after the score computation. In CUDA, `__syncwarp()` is a barrier for threads within a warp (convergent threads). For a block of 32 threads (exactly one warp), `__syncwarp()` should be sufficient. But actually, since we only have one warp and no divergence before the __syncwarp (assuming all threads are active), the writes to shared memory by lane 0 should be visible to other threads after `__syncwarp()`. Let me also reconsider: in the score computation loop, for `key_idx = 0`, all threads compute `dot` and reduce. Lane 0 writes `scores[0]`. For `key_idx = 1`, lane 0 writes `scores[1]`. By the end of the loop, all `scores[0..seq_len-1]` have been written by lane 0. Then `__syncwarp()` ensures all threads in the warp see all these writes. Actually, there's a subtle issue. `__syncwarp()` only ensures that threads within the warp have completed their memory accesses and are converged. It doesn't specifically flush writes to shared memory. But in practice, within a single warp, writes to shared memory are visible to other threads after a few instructions, and `__syncwarp()` is sufficient for correctness. An alternative is to use `__threadfence_block()` after the loop, but `__syncwarp()` should be enough for a single warp. Kernel 4: attn_out_kernel ```cuda __global__ void attn_out_kernel( const float* __restrict__ attn_out, const float* __restrict__ residual, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ W_O, const float* __restrict__ b_O, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int nthread = blockDim.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; __shared__ float temp[256]; __shared__ float shared_sums[4]; // Load attn_out into shared memory if (tid < hidden) { temp[tid] = attn_out[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Output projection + residual for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden; out_idx += nthread) { float sum = b_O[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += temp[i] * W_O[i * hidden + out_idx]; } sum += residual[token_idx * hidden + out_idx]; temp[out_idx] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm if (tid == 0) { float mean = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) mean += temp[i]; mean /= hidden; shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float diff = temp[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= hidden; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (temp[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } ``` Kernel 5: ffn_kernel ```cuda __global__ void ffn_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, const float* __restrict__ W_inter, const float* __restrict__ b_inter, const float* __restrict__ W_out, const float* __restrict__ b_out, const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma, const float* __restrict__ ln_beta, int seq_len, int hidden, int intermediate_size) { int token_idx = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int nthread = blockDim.x; if (token_idx >= seq_len) return; extern __shared__ float ffn_smem[]; float* input_shared = ffn_smem; float* inter_shared = ffn_smem + hidden; float* temp_shared = ffn_smem + hidden + intermediate_size; float* shared_sums = ffn_smem + hidden + intermediate_size + hidden; if (tid < hidden) { input_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid]; } __syncthreads(); // Intermediate for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < intermediate_size; out_idx += nthread) { float sum = b_inter[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { sum += input_shared[i] * W_inter[i * intermediate_size + out_idx]; } sum = 0.5f * sum * (1.0f + erff(sum * 0.70710678118f)); inter_shared[out_idx] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Output + residual for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden; out_idx += nthread) { float sum = b_out[out_idx]; for (int i = 0; i < intermediate_size; i++) { sum += inter_shared[i] * W_out[i * hidden + out_idx]; } sum += input_shared[out_idx]; temp_shared[out_idx] = sum; } __syncthreads(); // Layer norm if (tid == 0) { float mean = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) mean += temp_shared[i]; mean /= hidden; shared_sums[0] = mean; } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 1) { float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) { float diff = temp_shared[i] - mean; var += diff * diff; } var /= hidden; shared_sums[1] = var; } __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_sums[0]; float var = shared_sums[1]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f); if (tid < hidden) { output[token_idx * hidden + tid] = (temp_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid]; } } ``` Wait, for the FFN kernel with dynamic shared memory, I need to pass the total size: `hidden + intermediate_size + hidden + 4` floats. callcompile_kernel { "kernel_code": "import torch\nfrom transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig\nfrom torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline\n\nCUDA_CODE = r'''\n#include <torch/extension.h>\n#include <cuda_runtime.h>\n#include <cmath>\n\n// Embedding kernel: lookup -> layer norm -> projection\n__global__ void embed_kernel(\n const int64_t* __restrict__ input_ids,\n float* __restrict__ output,\n const float* __restrict__ word_embed,\n const float* __restrict__ pos_embed,\n const float* __restrict__ type_embed,\n const float* __restrict__ ln_gamma,\n const float* __restrict__ ln_beta,\n const float* __restrict__ proj_weight,\n const float* __restrict__ proj_bias,\n int seq_len, int vocab_size, int embed_dim, int hidden_dim) {\n \n int token_idx = blockIdx.x;\n int tid = threadIdx.x;\n int nthread = blockDim.x;\n \n if (token_idx >= seq_len) return;\n \n __shared__ float x_shared[256];\n __shared__ float shared_sums[4];\n \n int64_t token_id = input_ids[token_idx];\n \n if (tid < embed_dim) {\n x_shared[tid] = word_embed[token_id * embed_dim + tid]\n + pos_embed[token_idx * embed_dim + tid]\n + type_embed[tid];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n \n float mean = 0.0f;\n if (tid == 0) {\n for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) mean += x_shared[i];\n mean /= embed_dim;\n shared_sums[0] = mean;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n mean = shared_sums[0];\n \n float var = 0.0f;\n if (tid == 1) {\n for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) {\n float diff = x_shared[i] - mean;\n var += diff * diff;\n }\n var /= embed_dim;\n shared_sums[1] = var;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n var = shared_sums[1];\n \n float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-12f);\n \n if (tid < embed_dim) {\n x_shared[tid] = (x_shared[tid] - mean) * inv_std * ln_gamma[tid] + ln_beta[tid];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n \n for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden_dim; out_idx += nthread) {\n float sum = proj_bias[out_idx];\n for (int i = 0; i < embed_dim; i++) {\n sum += x_shared[i] * proj_weight[i * hidden_dim + out_idx];\n }\n output[token_idx * hidden_dim + out_idx] = sum;\n }\n}\n\n// QKV projection kernel\n__global__ void qkv_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ input,\n float* __restrict__ q,\n float* __restrict__ k,\n float* __restrict__ v,\n const float* __restrict__ W_Q,\n const float* __restrict__ b_Q,\n const float* __restrict__ W_K,\n const float* __restrict__ b_K,\n const float* __restrict__ W_V,\n const float* __restrict__ b_V,\n int seq_len, int hidden) {\n \n int token_idx = blockIdx.x;\n int tid = threadIdx.x;\n int nthread = blockDim.x;\n \n if (token_idx >= seq_len) return;\n \n extern __shared__ float smem[];\n float* x_shared = smem;\n \n if (tid < hidden) {\n x_shared[tid] = input[token_idx * hidden + tid];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n \n for (int out_idx = tid; out_idx < hidden; out_idx += nthread) {\n float q_sum = b_Q[out_idx];\n float k_sum = b_K[out_idx];\n float v_sum = b_V[out_idx];\n for (int i = 0; i < hidden; i++) {\n float val = x_shared[i];\n q_sum += val * W_Q[i * hidden + out_idx];\n k_sum += val * W_K[i * hidden + out_idx];\n v_sum += val * W_V[i * hidden + out_idx];\n }\n q[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = q_sum;\n k[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = k_sum;\n v[token_idx * hidden + out_idx] = v_sum;\n }\n}\n\n// Attention kernel: one warp per head per query position\n__global__ __launch_bounds__(32) void attention_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ q,\n const float* __restrict__ k,\n const float* __restrict__ v,\n float* __restrict__ attn_out,\n int seq_len, int hidden, int num_heads, int head_dim) {\n \n int token_idx = blockIdx.x;\n int head = blockIdx.y;\n int lane = threadIdx.x;\n \n if (token_idx >= seq_len || head >= num_heads || lane >= 32) return;\n \n int head_offset = head * head_dim;\n int elem0 = head_offset + lane * 2;\n int elem1 = elem0 + 1;\n \n float q0 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem0];\n float q1 = q[token_idx * hidden + elem1];\n \n __shared__ float scores[512];\n const float scale = rsqrtf((float)head_dim);\n \n for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) {\n float k0 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem0];\n float k1 = k[key_idx * hidden + elem1];\n float dot = q0 * k0 + q1 * k1;\n \n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2)\n dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset);\n \n if (lane == 0)\n scores[key_idx] = dot * scale;\n }\n \n __syncwarp();\n \n float local_max = -1e9f;\n for (int i = lane; i < seq_len; i += 32)\n local_max = fmaxf(local_max, scores[i]);\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2)\n __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_sum, 0);\n float inv_sum = 1.0f / sum_exp;\n \n float out0 = 0.0f;\n float out1 = 0.0f;\n for (int key_idx = 0; key_idx < seq_len; key_idx++) {\n float prob =
